        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319044522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4655864337995993466">THIS WAS SUPERFANTABULOUS!!!! I don't even know where to begin describing my feelings! I thought <i>Storm</i> was incredible......*shaking head*......Gabriel just up and ran away with my heart! <i>Spark</i> blew me away......like seriously...out of the ball park, blew me away! It was simply amazing! <b>Ms. Kemmerer you are totally, hands down and undeniably my 2012 girl crush! :D</b> Woman, I just freakin LOVE YOU! <br/><br/><b>
  <u>UPDATE!!!</u>
</b><br/><br/><i>****First and foremost, I would like to thank Brigid Kemmerer for providing me with a cop</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4655864337995993466" style="display:none">THIS WAS SUPERFANTABULOUS!!!! I don't even know where to begin describing my feelings! I thought <i>Storm</i> was incredible......*shaking head*......Gabriel just up and ran away with my heart! <i>Spark</i> blew me away......like seriously...out of the ball park, blew me away! It was simply amazing! <b>Ms. Kemmerer you are totally, hands down and undeniably my 2012 girl crush! :D</b> Woman, I just freakin LOVE YOU! <br /><br /><b>
  <u>UPDATE!!!</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>****First and foremost, I would like to thank Brigid Kemmerer for providing me with a copy of her book for review! I wouldn’t have melted into a puddle of goo without you! So, thank you!****</i><br /><br /><b>HOLY MOTHER OF ALL TURTLES!!!</b><br /><br />I’m weak in the knees, delirious from too much hotness in one book, drooling like a clown on crack over Gabriel Merrick and I think I might have passed out at some point too!<br /><br />After reading <i>Spark</i>, this is the only...and I repeat <i>only</i> conclusion I have drawn:<br /><br />*raises right hand* <b>I solemnly swear on the unfairness of all hot guys being fictional that <i>Spark</i> will drown you in emotions and all it’s greatness! It is hazardous to your health. Proceed at your own risk.</b><br /><br />And now that is out of the way....<br /><br />Where do I even begin with this book?? I’m flying in the clouds from all my giddiness over <i>Spark</i>! It was just ridonculously hot - (pun intended ;)! I fell in love all over again with the world Ms. Kemmerer has created and with the Merrick brothers. It had everything, I had hoped the sequel to an amazing book like <i>Storm</i> would have and much more. There was action, mystery, suspense, thrill, deep emotions beyond belief, humor and scorching romance - adding up to one fantastic and addicting story! <i>Storm</i> left me speechless and blown away but <i>Spark</i> did all that and had my heart beating a mile a minute too! I just couldn’t put it down! :D<br /><br /><i>Spark</i> picks up where <i>Storm</i> left off. Ms. Kemmerer doesn’t hesitate to plunge her readers into the action and I really enjoyed that. The story gets you completely hooked from page one. I was anticipating what would happen next after every chapter I finished...but still could not contain my gasp of surprise with all the unexpected twists and turns! The storyline was thrilling and I enjoyed it very much! <br /><br />One of the most noticeable things about Ms. Kemmerer’s writing is the facts underlying the characters and relationships. In <i>Spark</i>, there was a lot of depth to the characters’ feelings which made them all the more realistic. I had no trouble connecting with Becca or even Gabriel, and I was very sympathetic with all that they are going through. But what I really enjoy about this series is the fact that Ms. Kemmerer’s characters’ emotional problems don’t all focus around the supernatural but are teenage issues. I love that!<br /><br />I loved Gabriel in <i>Storm</i>, and to have his perspective in <i>Spark</i> was a dream come true! <b>I am officially...Gabriel Merrick’s personal pimp!</b> I was prepared for a tough bad boy with a tendency to spout off snarky remarks, but man, I was NOT prepared for a <i>vulnerable</i> Gabriel Merrick. Gabriel goes through so much in this book that I just wanted to give him a big teddy bear squeeze. You understand Gabriel’s reasons behind his impulsive and reckless behaviour and I just cried for his loneliness. D: I felt ALL of his emotions and all that emotional angst...it felt as if my heart was being ripped out of me. But he learns to deal with his emotions, problems, and element, and I loved his strength to keep trying despite being blamed for things he didn’t do and his brothers “against him”! Not to mention that he is sex on two legs...kinda makes him hard to resist! *fans self* I had no doubt that Gabriel would make my heart flutter....and boy did he ever!<br /><br />As for Layne....she is the polar opposite of Gabriel. Shy, quiet, responsible and nerdy. But she also carried a lot of emotional baggage, the kind that makes your heart hurt and makes your eyes blur with tears. Despite being opposites, the one thing they both shared were their insecurities and in the end they were just perfect for each other. What I loved most about Layne was her compassion to help Gabriel despite him being a jerk-face. She saw through his tough facade, and truly understood him. They were beautiful together, and they believed in each other - which was what got them through all the shit in their lives. Another inspiring quality about Layne was her constant support of her brother Simon. I loved how she always took care of him. She was adorable and I LOVED HER!!<br /><br />Then the relationship....that was just fiery! HOT DAMN! Gabriel and Layne together with their emotions all thrown in the mix, the romance was sky rocketing through the roof! It was steamy, sexy, scorching and just simply electrifying. From their witty and snarky remarks to their passionate kisses, Gabriel and Layne will have you biting your knuckles and wishing you were sitting under a cold shower! It was that HOT! And you just can’t help but want more! *fanning self*<br /><br />The other characters were all there as well. Hunter was an unlikely ally and I was cheering him on for being there for Gabriel. As for Nicky..well..I was aching with all that was happening between him and Gabriel, but was touched by their strong bond. The one thing, I’m not sure about anymore is Nick’s relationship with Quinn. I did like her in <i>Storm</i> but I just don’t see them together anymore. But, I’m still keeping an open mind. Now, the award......goes to Michael! He was like an angel in the hell of Gabriel’s life. I loved how his relationship with Gabriel improves like a million times over....so kudos to you Michael for not being an ass-hat but being a true brother! :D<br /><br />Overall, Brigid you have totally won my heart! You have given the YA fans something beyond imaginable - a riveting and engaging series! <i>Spark</i> was full of emotion, heart pounding action, thrilling mystery and panty melting romance! The way Ms. Kemmerer writes, every chapter was sensational and it was impossible to put down! The wonderful characters will enthrall you and pull you into their world...and you wont want to leave anytime soon! I definitely recommend this to all YA fans, and if you enjoyed <i>Storm</i>, you will love and lust after <i>Spark</i>. Brigid Kemmerer, don’t you dare stop writing this amazing series! I can’t wait to get my hands on <i>Spirit</i> next! Simply <b>phenomenal!</b><br /><br />And for all those who haven't read this series yet, I don't give two shakes of a rat’s ass, what you are doing...<b>GET UP AND GO GET THE BOOK NOW!</b> Okay, I'm done...*sweet smile* <br /><br />This review is also posted at <a href="http://loveaffairwithabookreviews.blogspot.ca/2012/08/review-spark-elemental-2-by-brigid.html#more" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary Love Affair</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4655864337995993466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_329434787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329434787" />
    <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda"><img alt="Jessica Buwalda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600119200p2/6926261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/329434787?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Buwalda" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda">Jessica Buwalda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6926261-jessica-buwalda?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6926261-jessica-buwalda?shelf=first-reads-arcs">first-reads-arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329434787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1000035097435710299">Holy baby jesus. I can’t believe I got my hands on an ARC of this bad boy. I think my knees may have given way when I realized that I had it. I may have snapped out of it and started doing the cancan for good measure then raced over to the lounger and clicked on the power to my beautiful KOBO.<br/>For any one out there that has a KOBO and downloaded a book in PDF format onto it they understand my pain when I say usually it prevents you from reading the book until you can find it in some other source.</span>
  <span id="freeText1000035097435710299" style="display:none">Holy baby jesus. I can’t believe I got my hands on an ARC of this bad boy. I think my knees may have given way when I realized that I had it. I may have snapped out of it and started doing the cancan for good measure then raced over to the lounger and clicked on the power to my beautiful KOBO.<br />For any one out there that has a KOBO and downloaded a book in PDF format onto it they understand my pain when I say usually it prevents you from reading the book until you can find it in some other source. <br />Well, obviously I was desperate because I thought, “screw this business” and read it anyway. Hardships and all.<br />FYI, there is always something good in getting an ARC. But, there is also something bad in getting an ARC of a series. My reason behind this is love this series. I finished Spark and turned the pages for the ‘sneak peak’ of Spirit and read the couple of pages that were there and when I flipped the page and saw a blank one I realized “Crap. Now I have to wait until May of 2013 to read the rest of it. That’s 10 MONTHS away.” It makes me want to take a cold shower fully clothed and rock in the corner while crying. That is the only bad thing about receiving an ARC of a book in a series. <br />But then again I guess I have to two that I re-read and snuggle with at night until the third one comes out. <br />Yeah. I will just dream about Chris, and Gabriel. Hell, Nicky too. Oh alright I think I have room to dream about Michael too. Well might as well throw Hunter in there too especially since my mind will be filled with him when the next one is released. Jeeze these boys are going to take up some of my mind space. Oh!! And there’s still Fearless (Elementals #1.5) Hehehehe.<br />The first book was about Chris and Becca, and now we get Gabriel and Layne. And they are a whole other bowl of coco puff trouble. In the first book Gabriel was a jerk, but defended people when he got to know them. Well…he still is a major jerk in this novel. But you learn everything that’s behind his anger. I mean can you blame him for being angry and guilt ridden after everything that has happened with his parents and Nick?<br />Oh Gabriel. I cried for you. I also lusted for you and your firey hot skin. And every time you opened your mouth and the inevitable garbage came spewing out I thought, “Why Gabriel. Why? I know you’re one of those big teddy bears you win at the fair. Come on. I know it.” But, can you blame him? His element is fire. Its not exactly easy to control fire, not to mention he would have to be around it all the time in large amount to learn how to control it and it’s not like he can run around setting things on fire in large quatities. And we realize that his element actually scares him. You finally get your hands on a completely different Gabriel, the one that he hides under all his angst, anger, and loneliness. But I guess that is where Layne comes in. They push each other and it made me freakin’ smile like a jackal. And then there is everything that happens with Michael and him. And well you would think they were brothers. There was some Kodak moments there. Hehehehe.<br />Good:<br />Gabriel: HHAAWWWTT. Obviously. So are his brothers. But there is a hero in their just wanting to be in his element and rise up. This is the guy who beats up his fellow teammates seconds after learning they did something bad to a girl. I do have to question how he can leave so many bloody faces and not get arrested…well for assault I should say.<br />Layne: She’s cool! We finally get a nerd in the bunch! AND who would have thought that the butt ogling Mr. Jock of the brothers would be the one to take notice. Fist pump to all the nerdy girls who love to read and have glasses.<br />Simon: He is one cool guy. I have mad respect for not letting this get in his way of enjoying life.<br />Michael: I just want to kiss you out of sheer happiness. You rock in this book. Glad you took the ass-hat cap off and put on the big brother cap instead.<br />Bad: <br />I miss Chris. Oh, Chris. You will always been the first Merrick brother I loved. Let face it the first book Hunter got in the way of Chris and Becca, and I was hoping that we would get some Chris and Becca in this book. We did…a little, but not enough. I demand another book…with Chris and Becca. Ou! A fourth book in the series? Yes please! And another, maybe with Nicky? I can see all the people out there closing their eyes and being tight lipped while nodding their heads in complete agreement.<br />Overall (Writing style, story line, and general):<br />Overall I love Brigid’s writing. I love her characters that are so full of depth. I absolutely love how I thought Gabriel was going to make one choice that was completely Gabriel and then surprised to find that he choose something else. I cried, I felt the pain in my heart when I realized how lonely Gabriel was. No other one has the difficulties like he does with his elemental. All other elements are not naturally dangerous. My Brigid Kemmerer brings across the pain and guilt and every other emotion that is wrapped up inside Gabriel Merrick with what seems like ease. The book surrounds you with emotion and you can picture everything perfectly. I never once thought I had read something wrong or couldn’t understand were the character was coming from. Brigid Kemmerer has created people in her stories that you could believe actually existed. That is how freaky good she is.<br /><br />View more of my review and others at my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com">www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1000035097435710299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_675960693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/675960693" />
    <a title="Irina Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena"><img alt="Irina Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587303756p2/7664770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/675960693?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irina Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irina Elena" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena">Irina Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780758280060" href="/book/show/13616050-spark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=paranormal-or-urban-fantasy">paranormal-or-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=ya-pnr">ya-pnr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer675960693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4775863710414663440">Wow. No snark for this one; I've only got praise.<br/><br/>It took me (much) less than 12 hours to read this one - and that includes eating, sleeping and convincing a bunch of people to <i>just stop talking to me already</i>. Just to give you an idea of how much I liked it.<br/><br/>If I had a favourites shelf - which I don't because my favourite books change with the weather - this would go straight in there.<br/><br/>Much more intense and mature than the first book and novellas in the Elemental series, this one perfectly captured</span>
  <span id="freeText4775863710414663440" style="display:none">Wow. No snark for this one; I've only got praise.<br /><br />It took me (much) less than 12 hours to read this one - and that includes eating, sleeping and convincing a bunch of people to <i>just stop talking to me already</i>. Just to give you an idea of how much I liked it.<br /><br />If I had a favourites shelf - which I don't because my favourite books change with the weather - this would go straight in there.<br /><br />Much more intense and mature than the first book and novellas in the Elemental series, this one perfectly captured all the anger, frustration, loneliness and pent-up energy of adolescence - and what better element to express them than fire?<br />Gabriel is much more complex and vulnerable than I'd expected. In the first parts of the series we only got to see him through the eyes of other characters, to whom he seems more of an arrogant jackass than anything else. Now, delving into his own thoughts and feelings for the first time, I got to see how much pain and self-blame he's enduring, and my heart broke for him. He is, officially, one of the best written male teenagers I've ever encountered in any book. I'm being serious here. It's not just that he's hot and snarky and just plain fun - although, well, yeah.<br /><br />All of the characters in this book are well-rounded, fully developed and complex, and each of them has specific problems and thoughts and expectations and ways of coping with what life and people throw at them.<br />Their lives intersect and influence each other continuously, just the way it happens irl, and the process was masterfully rendered in all its nuances.<br />As if that weren't enought, I got to delve even deeper into the Merrick brothers' relationship and see how deeply each of them affects the others, how they hurt and help each other, how they love each other so much that I'm reminded of why I always wanted siblings.<br />The more complex character dynamics don't only show within the Merrick family, but also between other characters like Layne, Simon, Becca's father and Hunter. I know I haven't been nice to him in the past: I thought he was creepy and dishonest and weird and he kind of freaked me out. Well, <i>nevermind all that</i>. He's <i>awesome</i>. He's a loyal friend, a scarred boy and a scheming bastard. I can't wait to read his story. And Nick's. And Michael's. Can I have more after these?<br />One more point in this series' favour is that each book concentrates on one love story, but its happenings involve all the characters around the two MCs, so each novel ends up being a choral story.<br /><br />The romance: will you just <i>look</i> at that? A pnr YA het romance is what this is, and I loved it.<br />We have the not-very-original couple of 1 girl with stone walls around her, keeping her distance from everyone and particularly from her love interest + 1 bad boy showing his vulnerable side for the first time but without much hesitation because he knows she's the one = magic stuff. Because it was done realistically and it was explored deeply, so I believed it and loved it.<br />The fact that there was no useless angsting and wondering about the supernatural element helped a lot. That, in its turn, was helped by some, er, particular circumstances that made the situation pretty clear to Layne - hey, I'm trying not to spoil here, okay? That's a deus ex machina I despised, but really, it's buried under so much awesomeness and perfection that I just left it hidden down there. Layne herself is a wonderful character and I even loved her insecurities, because they were coupled with great strengths and because they weren't there just for their own sake, but to show what she'd been through.<br />Both she and Gabriel grew all throughout the book, thanks to each other and to other characters, and the love story was all the more believable because of that.<br /><br />In short, everything here was more mature, intense, complex and visually powerful than the previous books - as if the author had suddenly had a writerly growth spurt - yet showed the teenage... world? Yeah, let's sound like a children's book critic - with laser-like precision.<br />Then there was the suspense - I was literally on the edge of my seat. I never do that. I'm usually lying down when I read, but at one point I was just walking around with my phone in a death grip because my ereader was dead (I always notice these things at the last possible minute) and I could not stop reading <i>there</i>.<br />And then there were scenes like this one:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Layne wanted to be brave. She wanted to be optimistic.<br />But she started crying anyway.<br />Nick's hand went over hers.<br />"Gabriel will find us. He'll get us out."<br />"How?" she choked. "How do you know?"<br />"Because he always does."</i>
</blockquote><br />... that you probably won't even get because you have no idea what's going on, but I was just this tight little trembling ball of emotion.<br /><br />---<br /><br />*laughs* Okay, don't panic; there <i>are</i> some coherent, complete and comprehensible reviews of this book to be found on the Internet. I'll save you the work and send you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/376388028" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br />Forgive me, I've just woken up and I just had this mess of a review bubbling in my brain. I hope it conveyed all my love and awe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4775863710414663440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_376569167" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/376569167" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/376569167?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer376569167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8704676615914959680"><br/>By now you’ve probably seen lot of reviews out there for Spark, raving about the <b>SERIOUSLY HOT BOYS</b>. Well that’s certainly no exaggeration, there are four, and they ARE hot. But the draw for these stories is much more than that. The Elemental series is seriously cool with all of the Merrick brothers able to harness and control a different element: fire, water, air, earth. These boys are each a hero in their own right, yes, even cocky Gabriel, just waiting for the opportunity to get out. <br/><br/>Spark ce</span>
  <span id="freeText8704676615914959680" style="display:none"><br />By now you’ve probably seen lot of reviews out there for Spark, raving about the <b>SERIOUSLY HOT BOYS</b>. Well that’s certainly no exaggeration, there are four, and they ARE hot. But the draw for these stories is much more than that. The Elemental series is seriously cool with all of the Merrick brothers able to harness and control a different element: fire, water, air, earth. These boys are each a hero in their own right, yes, even cocky Gabriel, just waiting for the opportunity to get out. <br /><br />Spark centers on Gabriel, the hot-head twin of the Merrick brothers. Nick, the other half is the “good twin”: a whiz at school, kind to others and never gets into trouble. Gabriel is basically the exact opposite. He’s got a quick temper, always pushing limits, and he’s about to fail math, which is where Layne comes in. <br /><br />In math class, Layne sits right in front of Gabriel, and has always noticed him. She wonders what it would be like for Gabriel to notice a girl like her, and she’s about to find out. Layne dresses conservative in turtle necks, jeans, braided hair, and glasses. Definitely not the type Gabriel usually notices. <br /><br />The action and abilities of the Merrick boys is really fun to read about, but my favorite part of this story was the romance. No surprise for anyone who knows me! I loved the slow build between Layne and Gabriel. It was nice to see that Gabriel fell for Layne just the way she was, not because of some complete makeover that is a common device in romance novels. Instead, what captured his attention was her unexpected kindness. When he actually started looking at her, though, he realized even without the trendy, showy clothes, and perfectly applied makeup and styled hair, she was a beauty through and through. Oh this romance is SO sweet and there are so many swoony moments and scenes *sigh*. Here’s one to tempt you: <br /><br /><b>
  <i>”Do you want me to let you go?----She closed her eyes and nodded. A hesitation, and then, “I think you’re lying.” She was. But in what freakish world would a guy like Gabriel Merrick be standing with her in the dark, sharing kisses and secrets? He closed the space between them again, until the line of his body just brushed her. She couldn’t breathe. “Do you want me to let you go?” he said again. She swallowed. “No.” </i>
</b><br /><br />Oh my!<br /><br />Gabriel is still a little rough around the edges, that boy needs to get a handle on his temper! I wanted to shake him a few times because of it! But it stems mostly from feeling misunderstood and hurt by others, so I couldn’t help but give him a pass. He’s always felt like the worthless screw-up next to his brother, Nick. Layne recognizes Gabriel’s triggers and is good for him, just as he’s good for her. Layne has her own issues because of troubles at home. Plus, who doesn’t fall for a guy who sticks up for the bullied? Simon, Layne’s little brother is hearing impaired and Gabriel is so wonderful with him! Be still my heart! <br /><br />So take it from me. Pick this up sooner, rather than later! You’re bound to have a good time. <br /><br /><i>Thank you to Kensington and Netgalley for allowing me to read this.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8704676615914959680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2736339442" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2736339442" />
    <a title="Mary-ellen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8288505-mary-ellen"><img alt="Mary-ellen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377600080p2/8288505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2736339442?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary-ellen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary-ellen" href="/user/show/8288505-mary-ellen">Mary-ellen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2736339442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4680416030212029979">This is the second book in Brigid Kemmerer’s YA PNR series, Elemental.<br/><br/>It was much better than the first book. This one focuses on Gabriel Merrick, who was so angsty in book 1, I wasn’t sure I was going to enjoy this, but I ended up loving it. Getting inside Gabriel’s head gives a much better understanding of why he is the way he is and some of the choices he makes. Here he is a flawed but likeable character on a roller coaster of action, frustrations and misunderstandings. The romance is sweet a</span>
  <span id="freeText4680416030212029979" style="display:none">This is the second book in Brigid Kemmerer’s YA PNR series, Elemental.<br /><br />It was much better than the first book. This one focuses on Gabriel Merrick, who was so angsty in book 1, I wasn’t sure I was going to enjoy this, but I ended up loving it. Getting inside Gabriel’s head gives a much better understanding of why he is the way he is and some of the choices he makes. Here he is a flawed but likeable character on a roller coaster of action, frustrations and misunderstandings. The romance is sweet and we get to see all the characters from book 1.<br /><br />I’ll definitely be reading on.</span>

        <a class="right flag" rel="nofollow" id="flag_link2736339442" title="Flag this review as inappropriate." href="/flagged/new?resource_id=2736339442&amp;resource_type=Review&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F12977172-spark">flag</a>





      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_2736339442'><a id="like_count_review_2736339442" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/2736339442?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">15 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F12977172-spark">Like</a></span>

<div id="review_567832474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/567832474" />
    <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue"><img alt="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390185382p2/4659650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/567832474?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=paranormal-other">paranormal-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=blog-tour">blog-tour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=superheroes-superpowers">superheroes-superpowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=read-alongs">read-alongs</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer567832474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14633335029945765892">We're no longer Elemental virgins, but that doesn't mean the fun has to stop! As part of the <a href='http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/03/tour-sign-up-spirit-elementals-3.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Spirit Blog Tour</a> hosted by The Midnight Garden, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair' rel='nofollow noopener'>Steph</a> and I will be reading <i>Spark</i> for the next two weeks, so if you're still swooning over the Merrick boys with us, be sure to stop back here on May 12th to discuss! And if you had no restraint and tore through all the books already, we'd still love to hear from you. ;0) And if you're just joining us, check out the <a href='http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/04/elementals-read-along.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elementals Read Along sign up post</a> for mo</span>
  <span id="freeText14633335029945765892" style="display:none">We're no longer Elemental virgins, but that doesn't mean the fun has to stop! As part of the <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/03/tour-sign-up-spirit-elementals-3.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Spirit Blog Tour</a> hosted by The Midnight Garden, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair" rel="nofollow noopener">Steph</a> and I will be reading <i>Spark</i> for the next two weeks, so if you're still swooning over the Merrick boys with us, be sure to stop back here on May 12th to discuss! And if you had no restraint and tore through all the books already, we'd still love to hear from you. ;0) And if you're just joining us, check out the <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/04/elementals-read-along.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Elementals Read Along sign up post</a> for more details!<br><br>And don't forget, I'm giving away a SIGNED set of the first three Elementals books at the end of the <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/04/elementals-read-along.html" rel="nofollow noopener">read along</a>! Bonus entries for reviewing each book!<br><br><a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/04/elementals-read-along.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><a href="http://s34.photobucket.com/user/Jeannette29/media/cutting%20room%20floor/v-card-starry-eyed-revue_zps22f1aa2b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Elementals Read Along" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/522428.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>_______________________________________<br><br><b>*This review contains mild spoilers for <i>Storm</i>, the previous book in the Elementals series.*</b><br><br><b>**You do not have to read <i>Storm</i> to read this book. But I'd recommend it.  ;0)**</b><br><br>How very fitting that the brother with the shortest fuse is the one who controls fire?  I've jokingly been called a pyromaniac in the past, but I've got nothing on Gabriel.  And from what I've read so far, neither do any of his brothers!  ;0)<br><br>Chris's story in <i>Storm </i>was pretty great, but I found the moments featuring Gabriel to be the funniest...and some of my favorites, when he wasn't acting like a complete douche.  I knew there had to be some underlying reason for said douchiness because no one can harbor that much resentment without some basis for those feelings.  And there is.  Gabriel's temper stems from his own anger toward himself.  But instead of doing something about it, he turns it outward and takes all of his frustration out on his family.  It's a defense mechanism, and a pretty effective one at that.<br><br>I realize that some readers felt his character was chauvinistic and that he objectifies women based on comments made to or about Becca in the first book.  And, sure, he jumped to conclusions or made undue assumptions about her character without knowing her or any of the facts.  But he owns up to it.  He makes no excuses for his behavior and jumps to Becca's defense when he realizes he was wrong.  I knew he had it in him.<br><br>And, apparently, so did Layne.  She's the shy, studious girl that Gabriel's never even given a second look to...until one day when he needs to borrow a pencil.  This innocent gesture is a catalyst, a vehicle that brings about significant change in both of their lives.  But it takes them awhile to figure that part out.  I loved reading as they pulled back the layers, discovering each other's complexities and flaws.  Brigid Kemmerer writes about some seriously hot guys, but she also writes multifaceted characters that tug at your heartstrings with their sincerity and rub you the wrong way with their brazenness.<br><br>And then there are the powers she's given these kids.  And they actually use them!  Gabriel even <i>talks </i>to his element, convinces it to burn more intensely or pushes it back when it becomes too destructive.  It's all very entertaining.  But never more so than when Hunter decides they should be their own fire-fighting duo and save innocents from the arsonist who is plaguing their town at the moment.<br><br>That bromance between Gabriel and Hunter was so unexpected but <i>sooo</i> appreciated.  Gabriel feels like his family is against him at every turn, and Hunter's kind of the outcast of the group, having been spurned by Becca in favor of Chris.  (Okay, okay...maybe spurned is unfair...he was lying about who he was and that's hard to come back from.)  Anyway, it makes sense for them to become friends, and even though I didn't see it coming, I'm so glad for it.<br><br>I had so much fun while reading this book.  I swear there was a slap-happy grin plastered on my face the entire time I was reading.  I know the series isn't finished yet, and I don't want to take attention away from the other guys, but I think <i>Spark</i> just may go down as my favorite, with Gabriel being my favorite Elemental.  That said, I do have a soft spot for Hunter, and I don't really feel like I know Nick well enough to really judge him yet.  But look at all the pages I marked with favorite scenes or quotes!  I think it's pretty obvious I enjoyed this story quite a bit.<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2TUU9jMk-xk/UYrv7evnLOI/AAAAAAAAO0g/sgXi6bGjbII/s1600/spark-tagged.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380414376i/816913.jpg" width="149" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Favorite Quotes:</b><br><br>     “I can get my things,” said Gabriel.<br>     “I'm not letting you out of my sight.”<br>     Layne was caught between them, flustered. She was nearly wringing her hands. “Dad, it's not--”<br>     His eyes cut to Layne. “Now, Layne.”<br>     She swallowed and slinked past him into the living room.<br>     “Don't forget my box of condoms,” called Gabriel.<br><br>     Hunter sighed and gave him a look. “Come on, baby, don't be like that. Did you pack your midol?”<br>     “All right, all right.” Gabriel climbed out of the car, slamming the door behind him. “I don't even know why I like you.”<br><br>     She scowled out at the parking lot. “So is this like your <i>place</i>?”<br>     “My <i>place</i>?”<br>     “Where you bring girls.”<br>     “Yes. I bring girls to this run-down parking lot all the time.” He gestured with his cup. “I have a sign-up sheet nailed to that tree. Now that you mention it”--he glanced at his watch--“we should probably wrap this up.”<br><br>     But then Chris reappeared. He threw a glance at the wall that separated the lockers from the shower room. “Who's his sister?”<br>     Gabriel looked back in his bag and kept his voice nonchalant. “Just a girl in my math class.”<br>     “Just a girl, huh?”<br>     Gabriel glared at him. “Just a girl.”<br>     Chris smiled. “So was Becca.”<br><br><br><i>Thanks to Kensington for providing a copy for review! And thanks to <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a> for having me on the tour!</i><br><br>This review can also be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2013/05/elementals-read-along-review-spark-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.</span>

<div id="review_342452543" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/342452543" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/342452543?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer342452543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6532973022528332857">(4.5 stars)<br/><br/>After reading <i>Storm</i>, I couldn't help think how badly I wanted the next book already. So it was pretty funny and shocking to find this on Negalley. I didn't expect to read these books back to back, so to say I was pretty excited would be a huge understatement. <br/><br/>When I first read the blurb for Spark, I was eager to dive in to Gabriel's story since he seemed the most conflicted of the brothers, plus his power is fire so ya know it's gonna be good. But I was also slightly disappointed sinc</span>
  <span id="freeText6532973022528332857" style="display:none">(4.5 stars)<br /><br />After reading <i>Storm</i>, I couldn't help think how badly I wanted the next book already. So it was pretty funny and shocking to find this on Negalley. I didn't expect to read these books back to back, so to say I was pretty excited would be a huge understatement. <br /><br />When I first read the blurb for Spark, I was eager to dive in to Gabriel's story since he seemed the most conflicted of the brothers, plus his power is fire so ya know it's gonna be good. But I was also slightly disappointed since I wanted to see Chris and Becca's relationship play out through their point of views since we barley got to see it in Storm. Becca and Hunter, we got plenty of, which was a good thing, but Chris and Becca? Not so much which was a crying shame since I was rooting for him just as hard. I would have liked to see their story continue for at least one more book, but at last, this is Gabriel's story, so, moving on....<br /><br /><b>Spark</b> is a fiery and fierce sequel to the <i>Elemental</i> series. I'm not gonna lie, Gabriel is a hard character to like at times. He obviously has a lot of unresolved issues when it comes to his powers. He feels powerful and powerless at the same time. He's a runner and blames himself for almost everything. He has a really crappy attitude, he needed to calm the hell down throughout most of the book and the things he says and does were pretty cringe worthy stuff. In my experience with reading books, I find it easy to fall for the rebel, the bad guy, the underdog, but Gabriel makes the reader really work for it. I'm not saying this is a bad thing, in fact that's what I like the most about Gabriel and his brothers. They have these kick-ass powers, something supernatural, but they're still very much human. With human emotions and issues and baggage. They get their ass handed to them in spades and they even have to fight to get the girl. I can't tell you how refreshing these qualities are in characters I thought would be predictable from the start. So my point is, even though Gabriel is a very hard character to like, it's also pretty dame hard <i>not</i> to like him. These Merrick boys are frustrating as hell, but they all have such huge hearts and when push comes to shove they have each others backs and figure it all out together, even if it'll take the entire freaken series.<br /><br />I didn't have a chance to gush about these characters when I reviewed Storm since I basically geeked-out that I got to read the sequel two seconds after the first book, so I feel the need to say something about these delicious boys.<br />~Chris, I liked from the start. He's the youngest of the boys and doesn't quite have a hold of his powes yet, but you wouldn't know it. I love how he could pull strength from a storm and how his powers seem to enhance his personality, actually, that would have to go for all the brothers, a very genius move to incorporate elements that size up these characters personalities so amazingly well. I loved him in the first book. His emotions were so raw and real. I actually missed him in this book.<br />~Gabriel and Nick are twins. Gabriel is harsh and intense while Nick is the more grounded and kind. I love twin-connections. How you can feel so close to your sibling you wouldn't know how to breath without the other. I hated when they fought since I think they are stronger when together. <br />~Michael is the eldest and guardian since their parents death. The weight of responsibly is very visible and it takes it's toll. There is a big difference between being a father figure and being a big brother. Instead of getting to encourage recklessness and having fun, that a big brother has a right to dish out, he has to be the one to make sure these guys stay safe, which is hard since they always have someone looking for one wrong move. I didn't like Michael at first, but he really grew on me and now I actually respect him.<br />~Hunter was the easiest to swoon over. It only took the first words out of his mouth to know we were gonna get a long just fine. I liked his friendship with Gabriel in this one. I'm really looking forward to reading his novella and novel next. I just wish we didn't have to wait so long.<br />~Layne was a little hard to like at first. I liked Becca from the start, but Layne just has <i>so</i> much dame walls around her. Her defense is up so high I'm amazed that Gabriel could climb it. But as the story moves on you could tell that Gabriel and Layne were a perfect match. They balance each other out, challenge each other to be real and have a connection that know one could understand. It's a complex relationship sure, but it feels right. Plus, they also have some really intense sparks (pun intended) that made this even more fun to gush over.<br />~The only problem I had with this story was regards to Simon. I'm sorry, but what kind of asshat picks and tortures a deaf kid? I really hated those moments and wanted the prick that was doing it to just die already.<br />So wrong, on so many levels.<br /><br />I love the writing. Seriously, Brigid Kemmerer made this experience so effortless. It was like one of those love at first reads kinda thing. Instantaneously invested with each and everyone of these characters and the story line. It's fresh and exciting and a total blast to read.<br />Love, love love!<br /><br />Bottom line. This is my new favorite thing. I love the banter and brawls. I love that closeness that these brother share and I love watching them fall hard for girls that are the total opposite of themselves. I love that not once did I read the words "I love you". Everything was natural and exciting and simply fascinating. I can't get enough of this series and I can't wait to get my hands on the next book.<br /><br />An absolutely all consuming series from start to finish!!<br /><br />(Arc provided by Netgalley and Kensington publishing)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6532973022528332857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_380891019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380891019" />
    <a title="Lorenzio Phillibuster Fireworks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5133545-lorenzio-phillibuster-fireworks"><img alt="Lorenzio Phillibuster Fireworks" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/images/nophoto/user/c_111x148.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380891019?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorenzio Phillibuster Fireworks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorenzio Phillibuster Fireworks" href="/user/show/5133545-lorenzio-phillibuster-fireworks">Lorenzio Phillibuster Fireworks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781743310748" href="/book/show/13495069-spark">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380891019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13223595883924725705">If <i>Storm</i> was an explosion, <i>Spark</i> is an eruption. I don’t believe that I have ever felt <b>this</b> strongly for a character so quickly before. The Gabriel Merrick of <i>Storm</i> is a mischievous, smart arse identical twin. The Gabriel Merrick of <i>Spark</i> is a broken, hurt, troubled kid who’s an emotional live wire. <br/><br/><i>He’d been banned from the team, from a sport she knew he loved – God, even Simon practically worshipped Gabriel’s athletic ability. He was fighting with his twin brother, and they </i>had<i> to be close, th</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13223595883924725705" style="display:none">If <i>Storm</i> was an explosion, <i>Spark</i> is an eruption. I don’t believe that I have ever felt <b>this</b> strongly for a character so quickly before. The Gabriel Merrick of <i>Storm</i> is a mischievous, smart arse identical twin. The Gabriel Merrick of <i>Spark</i> is a broken, hurt, troubled kid who’s an emotional live wire. <br /><br /><i>He’d been banned from the team, from a sport she knew he loved – God, even Simon practically worshipped Gabriel’s athletic ability. He was fighting with his twin brother, and they </i>had<i> to be close, the way they seamlessly switched places in front of teachers and other students…<br />Layne took a deep breath. <br />Then she stepped forward to throw her arms around his neck and hug him. </i><br /><br />Nothing seems to be going right for poor Gabriel right now. He can’t control his element as well as his siblings, his maths teacher has discovered he’s been cheating since middle school, his love interest’s father accuses him of statutory rape, and his entire family seems to have turned against him and believe he’s capable of arson and murder. My heart was breaking for him, and I spent the entire book wanting to just jump into the pages and give the poor bastard a hug. Kemmerer has done an <b>amazing</b> job of getting you into the head of this 17 year old emotional wreck. <br /><br /><i>Gabriel didn’t move from the doorway. Everyone seemed to be getting along just fine.<br />Without him. </i><br /><br />Gabriel struggles with feelings of isolation for most of the novel, and it only made me want to hug him more. He blames himself for the death of his parents, for not protecting his twin, Nick, resulting in his kidnapping and broken leg, and feels like a failure because of his problems at school. He has no real friends outside of his family, and barely gets along with the parental figure in his life. As a result of feeling like an outsider, Gabriel is constantly on the defensive and often attacks in situations where you wish he wouldn’t. On so many occasions, I wanted to lock Gabriel up with his brothers and not let them out until they’d gotten all their aggression and feelings out in the open and then had a big hug and a cry. Kemmerer does a fantastic job of portraying Gabriel’s mood swings/temperamental behaviour. I constantly felt like I was on the edge of my seat, being attacked and just waiting for that perfect opportunity to take the first swing. <br /><br /><i>Christ, it felt fantastic to drive his fist into something. Especially when Hunter fought back with enough force to really make it worth it. <br /><br /><br />Gabriel wound his fingers around his lighter again. The potential for fire was </i>right there<i>, pulsing under his fingertips. <br /><br /><br />He could pick a fight. Get sent to the office. Alan Hulster sat to his left, and that guy was a tool. Gabriel wouldn’t even mind laying into him. </i><br /><br /><br />I found it a lot easier to connect with Layne than with Becca. This may possibly account for it: <br /><br /><i>She had a bookcase, white trimmed with pink, packed double and triple with paperbacks. No shocker there. It looked like she still had every book she’d ever read…More books threatened to fall from a pile on the nightstand. </i><br /><br />Layne is pretty awesome all around though. She loves her little brother, Simon, and does a lot to look after him. She’s been forced into the role of an adult after her mother abandoned them, and she’s got some pretty epic abandonment issues to match Gabriel’s. She’s also incredibly caring; she recognises Gabriel’s problem and tries very hard to help him for only <i>slightly</i> altruistic purposes (she thinks he’s a tad pretty). <br /><br />The mystery surrounding the novel of who exactly <i>is</i> the arsonist if it’s not Gabriel was <i>really</i> well done. I had my list of suspects and was completely blown away by who was <i>actually</i> involved. I’m now really looking forward to , released next year, to find out more about these mysterious new bad guys. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13223595883924725705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_399002491" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/399002491" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/399002491?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Isamlq by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer399002491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2777978491625340630"><b>4.5/5</b><br/><br/><b>This was really good.</b> I mean it, this was really, really good. In fact <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10401084-storm' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>STORM (Elemental #1,)</b>
</a> a book that took me totally by surprise in its awesomeness might even pale in comparison to this one. Who would have thought that stories of four hot brothers with super powers word turn out so good? So, if that first one was good, this one was so much better… perhaps because past the introductions, we get to have a closer look into what made one of them tick. Book One allowed us those introduct</span>
  <span id="freeText2777978491625340630" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5</b><br /><br /><b>This was really good.</b> I mean it, this was really, really good. In fact <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10401084-storm" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>STORM (Elemental #1,)</b>
</a> a book that took me totally by surprise in its awesomeness might even pale in comparison to this one. Who would have thought that stories of four hot brothers with super powers word turn out so good? So, if that first one was good, this one was so much better… perhaps because past the introductions, we get to have a closer look into what made one of them tick. Book One allowed us those introductions to the one who dealt in fire, in earth, in water and in air, but here it’s all Gabriel and his pain. I honestly thought there wouldn’t be much to him. In my mind it was as simple as this: secret pain = hot head. Except, his secret pain? It could get pretty angst-y painful indeed (and I’m not even being a smart ass about it right now.) The combination of him feeling the way he was then inconveniently overhearing something from someone else had my throat closing up for him. <br /><br /><b>Bad ass…</b>or perhaps the not so bad ass after all. Yes, this is just still action-filled as the first one. Yes, there’s more than one heart stopping sequence to do with fire here. And yes, we finally do witness Gabriel in action, but big shocker here: it’s his drama that sucked me in. When we first meet, it’s obvious he’s unhappy. And though normally the ‘everyone doesn’t get me; everyone is against me’ schitck would not be my thing, Gabriel’s moments had me lump-in-throat. He’s this reputation of being a screw up hot head… and apparently the boy bought into it as well. Here, it’s only made clear why. Factor in a growing gap between him and the one who has always been there with him beating himself up over things he couldn’t change. And I did hurt for him, save the fact that things could get frustrating in how typically <i>boy</i> his reactions were: close up and push out. <br /><br /><b>When I wasn’t feeling sorry for the guy, I was laughing…</b> because this book is mostly fun (though you probably couldn’t tell from how gushy I am over Gabriel’s drama.) <b>It is fun!</b> Take him and Layne, a pairing that’s initially an obvious one: straight A girl + hothead = LURV. And maybe it was obvious, but there is the fact that she’s her own baggage; that there are things she’s dealing with too. So them together was funny… with all that running away from then closing off; with all those thoughts of “does he/does she?..” Simply, they had me wondering (and laughing a little), why were they making it so hard?<br /><br /><b>A bit more interesting</b> is how the rest of them reveal more of themselves. Take Michael, when first introduced, he was all overbearing and controlling. He remains true to those, but all for good reason. Or Nick who’s always been good, well, not so stellar here. While the same brings him down, it made him more real too. Basically, he’s not prefect. Funny thing though: since Chris has had his <s>book</s> day in STORM, he’s barely here… and that’s fine too given it’s Hunter, boy with white streak in hair, who shines <i>again.</i> Hunter behaving the way did he proved that he was as good a catch as (if not better than ) Chris was… until he wasn’t anymore. Why? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He pulls the same stunt he did in book one, people! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> A fact that disappointed me greatly; still, I’m holding out because the teaser for BOOK THREE has me stoked. <br /><br /><b>Incredibly entertaining!<br />4.5/5</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2777978491625340630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_344487381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344487381" />
    <a title="Jasprit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit"><img alt="Jasprit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456315622p2/4841793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344487381?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasprit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasprit" href="/user/show/4841793-jasprit">Jasprit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=out-2012">out-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4841793-jasprit?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344487381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9223274531454107456">In Spark we are told the story from Merrick brother Gabriel, In Storm I just saw Gabriel as the hot headed cheeky Merrick brother, Chris had already played so much havoc with my heart in Storm that I didn’t think another Merrick brother would be able to sneak their way in, but boy was I wrong.<br/><br/>*contains some spoilers if you haven't read Storm*<br/>Now that the problems with the guide have been dealt with, the Merrick brothers can stay put, but under one condition that they don’t bring attention to the</span>
  <span id="freeText9223274531454107456" style="display:none">In Spark we are told the story from Merrick brother Gabriel, In Storm I just saw Gabriel as the hot headed cheeky Merrick brother, Chris had already played so much havoc with my heart in Storm that I didn’t think another Merrick brother would be able to sneak their way in, but boy was I wrong.<br /><br />*contains some spoilers if you haven't read Storm*<br />Now that the problems with the guide have been dealt with, the Merrick brothers can stay put, but under one condition that they don’t bring attention to themselves. Gabriel has a tough time dealing with this; he has a tough time dealing with anyone telling him what to do period. But especially now his control over his element is evolving there are only so many places he can practice without bringing everything burning down, plus with his brothers being able to control their elements that little bit more Gabriel feels left out. But then Hunter comes up with a suggestion, it’s risky but at least this way Gabriel can practice his element.<br /><br />I devoured Spark in one day, I don’t know what it is, Kemmerer just has a special way with words that lures you in, that you never want to leave. I was so disappointed when I’d finished this book as I have no idea when I’ll next get my Merrick brother fix I have to confess I may be a little bit enamoured by them to the point of obsession. Anyway I digress it was seriously something getting Gabriel’s pov. I love how with each book Kemmerer allows us to get to know each brother that little bit more. I was totally surprised by the side we were given of Gabriel, underneath all that bravado there is a true softy. Some of his scenes just shredded at my heart and others just made me melt. I don’t know why I had overlooked Gabriel in Storm, may be because I had Chris far too much on the brain, or maybe because of Gabriel’s snarky tendencies and his hot headedness. Previously I had thought that the scenes with Becca and Chris were sweet, but now I’ve come to the realisation that they don’t compare to some of the scenes between Gabriel and Layne. I know a lot of readers will be reconsidering Gabriel as their favourite Merrick brother after this.<br /><br />I enjoyed how in Spark we were able to move away from the issues that were integral in Storm. The focus was on something completely different and I thoroughly enjoyed it. I also liked how we got to see another side of Michael, he came across as a person who didn’t need to control everything, yes he was in Gabriel’s face a lot of the time, but he had loosened up a lot more since Storm.<br /><br />Again with Hunter I’m still confused where I stand with him, it was great he was helping Gabriel out, but I still felt he had his own agenda I don’t know why. I’m hoping the novella from Hunter’s pov will finally clear everything up.<br /><br />Kemmerer again hasn’t failed to disappoint me with her latest instalment; she has again left me wanting more. I can’t wait until my next Merrick fix.<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley and Kensington for the opportunity to read this book.<br /><br />This review and more can be found on <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.co.uk/2012/08/review-spark-by-brigid-kemmerer.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9223274531454107456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_344671729" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344671729" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3736122-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524600311p2/3736122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344671729?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/3736122-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=kindle-books">kindle-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344671729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1281187861692329395">t's not often that book 2 in a trilogy is better than the first, but that's definitely the case with Brigid Kemmerer's debut series. I mean, I liked Storm, but Spark exceeded any sort of expectations I had.<br/><br/>Mostly, this book is awesome because of Gabriel.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380181ra/737006.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I really loved his humor in Storm and was excited to read a book from his POV. And I was definitely not disappointed! He's one of my new favorite boys in YA, mostly because he's funny and has lots and lots of issues.<br/><br/>In fact, this whole book has l</span>
  <span id="freeText1281187861692329395" style="display:none">t's not often that book 2 in a trilogy is better than the first, but that's definitely the case with Brigid Kemmerer's debut series. I mean, I liked Storm, but Spark exceeded any sort of expectations I had.<br><br>Mostly, this book is awesome because of Gabriel.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380181ra/737006.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really loved his humor in Storm and was excited to read a book from his POV. And I was definitely not disappointed! He's one of my new favorite boys in YA, mostly because he's funny and has lots and lots of issues.<br><br>In fact, this whole book has lots of issues. The good kind. The kind that make characters well-developed and interesting, the kind that make you hurt for them even though you know they're not real. And Gabriel isn't the only one who's got some serious stuff he needs to work out - so does Layne.<br><br>Oh, Layne.<br><br>She really had to grow on me throughout the book because I wasn't a huge fan at the beginning. She's really closed off emotionally, and you can't help but wonder why Gabriel is interested in her. But as the story progresses and you learn more about her, it's hard not to totally fall in love with her; she's a great character, and she has some really good development throughout the story.<br><br>But like in Storm, the best relationships were between the Merrick brothers. I thought the drama in the family really hit a new level in this book when Gabriel gets angry at basically all of them. I loved his relationship with his twin brother Nick and how isolated he feels when Nick supposedly leaves him for other people. I loved the budding friendship between Gabriel and Michael, how they grudgingly love each other. The family drama is just SO GOOD!<br><br>OMG and the romance.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380380181ra/737007.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I already said I'm in love with Gabriel, right?<br><br>Okay, just making sure. Because really, his romance with Layne almost killed me. Even though the book takes place over the span of two weeks, I totally bought them together. I loved watching their progression, and ZOMG IT WAS JUST SO CUTE!<br><br>I adore super flawed characters and I adore it even more when said flawed characters get together. It's just like perfection.<br><br>Overall, this book was sort of different than Storm in that there isn't as much overt action. There's quite a bit with Gabriel exploring his fire element and interesting stuff with fires, but there are no outright fights between Elementals. But I honestly didn't miss the paranormal action at all because I thought this book was crafted and paced much better. Plus, Gabriel is the MC.<br><br>Oh wait...I already said that.<br><br>Something I found sort of ironic was that this book is so similar to Pushing the Limits by Katie McGarry, which released around the same time as this book. It's just weird that two books so similar (although one is contemporary and the other paranormal) would release so close together.<br><br>If you liked Storm, you'll definitely like this book. If you haven't read Storm, what are you doing?! Go read it now! There are 5 awesome book boys to fall in love with! Go thee hence and read a Brigid Kemmerer book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1281187861692329395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
