<div id="review_547641873" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/547641873" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/547641873?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=hot-and-funny-hero">hot-and-funny-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer547641873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3777100367481465245"><i>
  <b>4 STARS</b>
</i><br/><br/>I'm going to start this review with this HoYay (homoerotic...yay!) moment between Gabriel and Hunter:<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"You had a gun and you still fought me like that?"<br/>Hunter grinned. "Wait, you were fighting for real?"</i>
</b><br/><br/>Aren't they adorbs? No I'm not going to apologize for that word. <br/><br/>With how Gabriel was introduced in the first book, I was full on expecting more snark and more bite coming from the short-fused half of the Merrick Twins. This being his book had a lot of these endearing douchequotes b</span>
  <span id="freeText3777100367481465245" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>4 STARS</b>
</i><br /><br />I'm going to start this review with this HoYay (homoerotic...yay!) moment between Gabriel and Hunter:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"You had a gun and you still fought me like that?"<br />Hunter grinned. "Wait, you were fighting for real?"</i>
</b><br /><br />Aren't they adorbs? No I'm not going to apologize for that word. <br /><br />With how Gabriel was introduced in the first book, I was full on expecting more snark and more bite coming from the short-fused half of the Merrick Twins. This being his book had a lot of these endearing douchequotes but what was surprising was the emotional baggage behind all these verbal, and sometimes physical, blows he deals the people around him. He's more than a pretty face and a sharp tongue (mmm... Gabriel's tongue....)<br /><br />Though there was enough romance to drive the plot for this book, it's the relationship between the brothers that are very much brought to the fore. There are times when I am more interested in reading the scenes between Gabriel and his brothers than the ones he has with Layne (which is new for me, because I'm a romance reader first and foremost). I love reading the dynamics in Casa Merrick. Oh to be a fly on the wall in that house. I'm glad this installment explored the less predictable (compared to Nick) relationship between Michael and Gabriel. Their conversations were reined in (when they're not punching each other or breaking up a fight with another Merrick).No frills, no unnecessary drama, just subtle, matter-of-fact conversations without scrimping on the tugging at the heartstrings department. As how I would imagine men/boys of their age would talk. Or how they would argue or defend each other or come to blows. I have no brothers so this was all very fascinating for me.<br /><br />I'm not sure if I like Layne as much as I liked Becca though. I'm beginning to suspect the heroines in this series are going to be plot devices to save from elements-related danger and for the boys to play with their powers. And while I love reading about the action sequences, I do hope this changes up a bit. Layne was written a bit too much like a hodge-podge of the heroines I've read lately and Simon felt like a safety ploy to make sure I like Layne if all the hidden angst didn't pan out for me. I did like that she's smart and appreciate <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she didn't turn out to be an elemental too  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. So far, anyway. <br /><br />I'm enjoying the fact that the story is moving along in a direction that was totally unexpected for me (it went a little predictable for me in the first book). and has me curious as to what will happen next. Even if it's gonna be focused on Hunter. <br /><br />Sorry, but he eats using a plastic knife. To echo Gabriel's sentiments: Um, no.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3777100367481465245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17565560066799226479"><br/><b>2.5/5</b><br/><br/>After my vast enjoyment with <i>Elemental</i> I had high hopes for its sequel. I was especially excited because it features fan favourite Gabriel.   <span id="freeText17565560066799226479" style="display:none"><br /><b>2.5/5</b><br /><br />After my vast enjoyment with <i>Elemental</i> I had high hopes for its sequel. I was especially excited because it features fan favourite Gabriel. However it seems that Gabriel might have made a better secondary character than a leading man.<br /><br />The love story in this book was pretty weak. I hated Layne, she walked around with a stick in her butt, and was constantly running away from her problems. By running away I mean <b>literally</b> running away...and people thought Bella was terrible about confrontation.<br /><br />I found the plot to be pretty boring and just couldn't make myself care about what was happening. There were zero clues for the end twist, so it was completely out the blue and felt a little random. However I do like the direction that this series is going in and I will probably continue with it. I just hope that the next book has better heroes.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_605311295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605311295" />
    <a title="Crystal Navarro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180562-crystal-navarro"><img alt="Crystal Navarro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488685785p2/8180562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605311295?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Navarro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Navarro" href="/user/show/8180562-crystal-navarro">Crystal Navarro</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13616048-spark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180562-crystal-navarro?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180562-crystal-navarro?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180562-crystal-navarro?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605311295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer899588291610104109">Okay. Gabriel Merrick, you win. You are my favorite. You are soooo my favorite. You are a perfectly flawed ball of aeoghaoehgoaeaphe'a'! Wait, is that an oxymoron? You personify it. <br/><br/>I don't care about reading the rest of the series. Gabriel will always be my favorite. Don't tell me I will change my mind. I won't.<br/><br/><s>Stop it. Really, guys. I'M BEING SERIOUS. No really. I-- who cares if your favorite changes with every book and who cares if I keep loving old characters for new reasons I HAVE LAID CLAI</s></span>
  <span id="freeText899588291610104109" style="display:none">Okay. Gabriel Merrick, you win. You are my favorite. You are soooo my favorite. You are a perfectly flawed ball of aeoghaoehgoaeaphe'a'! Wait, is that an oxymoron? You personify it. <br /><br />I don't care about reading the rest of the series. Gabriel will always be my favorite. Don't tell me I will change my mind. I won't.<br /><br /><s>Stop it. Really, guys. I'M BEING SERIOUS. No really. I-- who cares if your favorite changes with every book and who cares if I keep loving old characters for new reasons I HAVE LAID CLAIM TO A FAVORITE AND FAVORITE HE WILL REMAIN.</s><br /><br />Welp, now that that is out of my system--<br /><br />This book worked for many reasons that I will list out into a pyramid diagram to explain the descent into ravenous love for Gabriel and this series.<br /><br /><b> Spark<br /> A light, temper<br /> Passion, flame, desire<br /> Rush, heat, chemistry, burning<br />Fire, hot, unpredictable, hot, Fire</b><br /><br />*ahem*<br /><br />LOL.<br /><br />Real review below:<br /><br /><i>Spark</i> has earned it's place on my favorites list for many reasons. The storytelling of Ms. Kemmerer is exemplary, engrossingly fast paced and relatable. That was the strongest point of this book. Gabriel was not my favorite character from Storm, and actually went a little under the radar. He won cool points for punching Drew in the face, but I still saw him exactly as Layne did in the beginning-- a thug who could get with anyone. And he acted the part as well, out of spite.<br /><br />Mmm, spite. Lets see how many flame-worthy words I can fit into this review. Gabriel embodies his element to a tee. <br /><br />We learn so much about Gabriel in this book -- so much more than we got on Chris in his book-- and his chemical reaction with Layne was exactly what I needed to finally understand him. Gabriel is not what he lets people believe him to be, he lets himself be viewed as such because his element is one of destruction, and all of experiences have proven to him that he cannot use it for good and that is why he is always messing up. The secret about Gabriel? He pretends he doesn't care when he cares <i>more than any other character in this series.</i> He wants to help, he wants to be worthwhile, and he wants to please others. He just can't, so he's given up, and allows himself to be set into a light that people are pleased to light him in.<br /><br />To the point he's convinced himself he's exactly that and he's afraid to let anyone see what he really is. To the point he hides the <i>good things he's done with so much fervor everyone gets the wrong idea.</i> He is so busy protecting other people he forgets to protect himself, or let anyone do it for him.<br /><br />And then <i>Layne</i> enters his world and that image goes up in flames. Explodes in his face. She just as fiery as he is, in her own right, and nothing like the other girls Gabriel has around him. She covers herself up completely. She is willing to help and put him in his place at the same time without a shred of regret. He's tempted, taunted, drawn to her almost exactly like he is his element-- she's got a spirit about her that mirrors him to a tee, and suddenly everything Gabriel forced himself to understand about who he was, or at least present, is bared and he's not sure how to take it. Fire is bright, it's blinding, is intense-- just like his uninhibited attraction to Layne, and her unintended passion for him.<br /><br />They both have a history with the flame, and while the one between them is fanned and grows, they learn that their connection-- to what they both fear and marvel at-- is going to draw them so close in so many ways.<br /><br />Gabriel comes to terms and control with his element-- and a newfound way to use his abilities for good. Fire fighting, and in love with a girl scarred from a house fire? Gabriel, you are so concerned at your brothers have a stronger connection to their element than you, when your element is <i>everything that you are not looking.</i><br /><br />I loved Layne. She is exactly the person Gabriel needs, to calm him down and stand toe-to-toe is with raging tempers and impossibly herioc overprotective streak. Gabriel is what she needs to loosen up and learn that a little adventure in life can ignite so many better things.<br /><br />Michael continues to earn cool points with me. His relationship with Hannah is endearing, considering it started with Gabriel, continued because of him, and now Gabriel is the first to know it's happening. He's shown himself to be growing more into his brother role-- but if this is because is growing or his brothers are becoming more understanding, I can't really pinpoint.<br /><br />Nicky-poo-- you and Gabriel really are twins. Absolutely compliments, even in your elements. Air can feed or tame a fire. Fire can choke the air or warm it. <br /><br />Hunter-- Okay, the friendship was <i>so</i> needed. Not sure what's going to happen with Hunter now, but I wonder if my reserved nature when it comes to his character is going to bite me in the butt later.<br /><br />And now, more fervent fan gushing--<br /><br /><s>How perfect was it how intense and powerful the physical relationship between Gabriel and Layne was? Just like fire. You get a little taste, and then it wants to consume it all.<br /><br />That can be taken so wrong. I need to stop myself.</s><br /><br />I wish we could have seen Layne's reaction to the truth! That is the only part that has me pouting. </span>
  <a data-text-id="899588291610104109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_338748906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/338748906" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/338748906?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer338748906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17580999572132693471">Rating: 3.5 Stars <br/><br/>When I went into <i> Spark, </i> I was 100% sure I would love it. Yes, 100%. Not even 99.9%. I devoured <i> Storm </i> in a matter of hours and after seeing <i> such </i> a huge string of glowing reviews for this book, I was confident that <i> for once </i> I wouldn't be the Black Sheep. Well, I was (unfortunately) quite wrong. I loved <i> Spark, </i> but ultimately, there was just something missing from it to make it a truly phenomenal novel. <br/><br/>First and foremost, I have to admit that I thought Gabriel was an ext</span>
  <span id="freeText17580999572132693471" style="display:none">Rating: 3.5 Stars <br /><br />When I went into <i> Spark, </i> I was 100% sure I would love it. Yes, 100%. Not even 99.9%. I devoured <i> Storm </i> in a matter of hours and after seeing <i> such </i> a huge string of glowing reviews for this book, I was confident that <i> for once </i> I wouldn't be the Black Sheep. Well, I was (unfortunately) quite wrong. I loved <i> Spark, </i> but ultimately, there was just something missing from it to make it a truly phenomenal novel. <br /><br />First and foremost, I have to admit that I thought Gabriel was an extremely well-written character. I could feel his loneliness, his desperation, and his confusion seeping through every page and once again, Brigid Kemmerer proves her talent in writing impeccable male POVs and realistic family dynamics. While I had already fallen in love with the Merrick brothers in <i> Storm, </i> I truly grew to appreciate Michael, Nick, and, of course, Gabriel. Plus, while I hated Hunter after <i> Storm, </i> I was glad that we were able to see a different side of him in this one which I really liked. Even Chris made his small appearances with Becca which were great, so once again, this is a family I am head-over-heels in love with. <br /><br />Layne, our female protagonist of <i> Spark, </i> is also an incredible heroine. She is intelligent, strong, and beautiful without trying to be. I think overall, Layne is much more likable character than Becca is, simply because she's the goody-two-shoes while Becca is more feisty. Still, I really liked both girls and I could understand Layne's tortured past and home life just as well as I could Gabriel's. Yet, their romance never won me over. For one, it was the extremely overdone and typically cliched bad-boy-falls-for-geek-math-tutor story line. While I didn't mind this too much, what I did mind was that I couldn't really <i> feel </i> for these two. I loved them as individual characters and I think their interactions together were sweet and they obviously understand one another very well, but I wasn't invested in their relationship at all. Plus, Layne isn't the type of girl I think anyone would expect Gabriel to fall for and unfortunately, Kemmerer was unable to really make me hop on their boat. I think compared to the sweet romance between Chris and Becca, I have to admit I was a tiny bit disappointed with the love story in this one. <br /><br />Yet another aspect of this novel that disappointed me was the lack of action in it. While the plot line of <i> Storm </i> revolves around the Guides, <i> Spark </i> is a much more mellow tale focusing on Gabriel’s character development and only hinting at a future clash with the Guides in the next installment. Thus, this unfortunately read like one of the many in-between novels which only serves to set up the plot of the next novel. In addition to that, I found the characterization of Layne’s parents, amongst a few other qualities of this story, to be extremely unrealistic. In my opinion, they were simply <i> too </i> evil and cartoon-ish to be real. <br /><br />What <i> really </i> made me dislike Spark though, was the lack of character development. Gabriel is hot-headed and he's constantly just a giant, raging mess of angst. Seriously, he slams doors, he runs ten miles, he yells, he punches people, he fights back. It's always constant <i> angst, </i> and while I understood it, after awhile it began to become annoying. Gabriel goes through a lot of experiences in this novel, especially with his brothers, and I wanted him to <i> learn </i> from them and become a better person who wasn't constantly fueled by his emotions, but even at the end, I just don't think he was. Yes, he gained mastery over his powers, but what about over himself? I still feel as if Gabriel could have grown and developed a little more in this one and the fact that I didn't see that as much as I would have liked was upsetting. <br /><br />Overall though, <i> Spark </i> is a great novel - I'm not refuting that. It has so much depth and the Merrick Brothers are truly phenomenal. While it lacked a lot of action, which I missed from <i> Storm, </i> and I wasn't totally invested in every aspect of it, I think most readers will love this. I, however, think I preferred <i> Storm, </i> but I can't wait for the next installment in this series either! :) <br /><br />You can read <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2012/10/review-spark-by-brigid-kemmerer.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on my blog <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings.</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17580999572132693471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_794376998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794376998" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/794376998?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780758280060" href="/book/show/13616050-spark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794376998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7723656169751512474">Wow, I was totally surprised by Spark, the 2nd book in the Elemental series by Brigid Kemmerer. Where the first book, Storm, was heart poundingly intense, I felt this book was sweeter. It pulled a little more on my heart strings but don’t get me wrong, there is still plenty of action. It begins directly where the previous book left off so you do need to have read Storm first.<br/><br/><a href='http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/fireonhand_zps748d943a.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387761505ra/7666686.gif' alt=' photo fireonhand_zps748d943a.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><br/>This book focuses on Gabe, half of the set of twins. Nick being the other half. Gabe’s element is fire. The fire spea</span>
  <span id="freeText7723656169751512474" style="display:none">Wow, I was totally surprised by Spark, the 2nd book in the Elemental series by Brigid Kemmerer. Where the first book, Storm, was heart poundingly intense, I felt this book was sweeter. It pulled a little more on my heart strings but don’t get me wrong, there is still plenty of action. It begins directly where the previous book left off so you do need to have read Storm first.<br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/fireonhand_zps748d943a.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387761505ra/7666686.gif" alt=" photo fireonhand_zps748d943a.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>This book focuses on Gabe, half of the set of twins. Nick being the other half. Gabe’s element is fire. The fire speaks to him, calls to him. He is working on his control of it but he’s not there yet. All of a sudden there is a rash of fires in their town and Gabe is suspected of setting them. But, he didn’t do it. No one believes him, not even his own brothers. He does find two very unexpected allies though. First is Hunter. A friendship is slowly developing between them. I really enjoyed seeing their friendship grow. They really needed each other and the support that only a friend can offer.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Dude. Seriously, if you start crying, people are going to think I’m breaking up with you.”</b>
</i><br><br>The other new relationship that is developing is with Layne. Layne is not the type of girl that Gabe would normally notice. She keeps herself fully covered in turtlenecks and is of the book smart type. But, when Gabe is failing math and the new substitute teacher is not going to cut him any slack, Layne comes to the rescue and offers to tutor him. But, Layne has a past of her own, secrets to hide. She needs Gabe as much as he needs her. <br><br>I think one of the sweetest aspects of this book, and the one that stole my heart is Layne’s younger brother, Simon. You see, Simon is deaf. He also LOVES basketball. The other kids at school bully Simon and who comes to his rescue but Gabe. In fact, Gabe’s brothers and Hunter also accept Simon without batting an eye. Simon even flourishes in their acceptance. The Merrick Brothers pushed themselves even deeper into my heart by the way they treated Simon.<br><br>Parts of this book broke my heart, though. Gabe is struggling with so much guilt. He blames himself for the death of his parents years ago. And he seems to blame himself for just about anything and everything that goes wrong. He feels like his twin, Nick is the perfect one. The one with all the brains. And the way Layne’s father treated him was appalling. There were times I just wanted to reach into the pages and hug him.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Surrounded by people, and he still felt so alone.”</b>
</i><br><br>I can’t say enough great things about these boys. We get hints of a future battle brewing between the Elementals and the Guides. And, there are many more questions to be answered. So I can’t wait to start the next book and find what’s next.<br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/wildfire_zps55a0e753.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387761505i/7666687.jpg" alt=" photo wildfire_zps55a0e753.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

<div id="review_325873780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/325873780" />
    <a title="Eunice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice"><img alt="Eunice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541224995p2/6078895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/325873780?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eunice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eunice" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice">Eunice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780758280060" href="/book/show/13616050-spark">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=arc-netgalley-edelweiss">arc-netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=death-tragedy-suicide">death-tragedy-suicide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=damn-gorgeous-males">damn-gorgeous-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=out-2012">out-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer325873780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5171329902577210033"><b>3.75 or 4 stars?? 4 stars!</b><br/><br/>I was so glad when I found out that it will be Gabriel's story in the second book of this series. He's my favorite among the Merrick brothers and to finally be able to see and learn more of him was just freaking awesome. And I just love how Brigid Kemmerer thoroughly explored Gabriel's characteristics here from being a friend, a brother, a student, a lover and a hero. <br/><br/>What I enjoyed most was seeing the soft and vulnerable sides of Gabriel, the side which he usually hide</span>
  <span id="freeText5171329902577210033" style="display:none"><b>3.75 or 4 stars?? 4 stars!</b><br /><br />I was so glad when I found out that it will be Gabriel's story in the second book of this series. He's my favorite among the Merrick brothers and to finally be able to see and learn more of him was just freaking awesome. And I just love how Brigid Kemmerer thoroughly explored Gabriel's characteristics here from being a friend, a brother, a student, a lover and a hero. <br /><br />What I enjoyed most was seeing the soft and vulnerable sides of Gabriel, the side which he usually hides through his tough facade. Here I was able to understand his reasons behind his impulsive, reckless and ill-tempered behavior. Much more to that was that I saw how much he actually valued his relationship with his family, especially with his twin brother, Nick. <br /><br />Behind his tough and easy-going exterior was a sensitive boy who had his own frustrations, insecurities, regrets and sadness brought by the extraordinary circumstances their family had. Gabriel struggled to control his element and to prove that it could be used to do good things too. However, things didn't go easy. Beings accused of things he didn't do plus not being entirely trusted by his brothers made it even harder for him. But still he did the right things; save the lives of other people and his loved ones even if it might press him more to the accusations. <br /><br />Layne was quite the opposite of Gabriel. Quiet, organized, responsible and patient. But what they had the same was the insecurities they had about their selves. Yet they fit each other, what's lacking with the other fills out by the other. Layne was a very genuine character and I love how she cared for his brother and how she didn't put up to any of Gabriel's sh*t during the earlier parts. <br /><br />I was able to learn more of the other Merrick brothers as well. I was actually touched by Gabriel and Nick's relationship although <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[they'd spent almost the entire time in this book not in good terms. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I was both impressed and sympathetic to Micheal especially with the things that he needed to do to keep his family safe and together. So I was really glad that by the end he got himself a girl *wink wink* Look out for that! And one more thing, I remember saying in my review in Storm that I didn't like Hunter, but after reading this, I think I'm really liking him! I love the camaraderie he and Gabriel shared here. <br /><br />I love how Kemmerer captured the very realistic problems and struggles a family could have especially in the circumstances of the Merrick brother. There were moments between the brothers that were very poignant and heartbreaking and moments that were uplifting and touching. It was different or rather refreshing and new since on all theses dramas boys were the one involved. It wasn't awkward and I think the author captured just the right ways and emotions and thoughts these guys would have. <br /><br />If you loved Storm, I'm sure you're gonna love this one even more. Brigid Kemmerer did a very wonderful job in writing an action-packed and thrilling paranormal book but with realistic and authentic teen and family problems with the hottest brothers in the YA world! lol! I recommend this book. :)<br /><br /><i>*Thank you Kensington and Netgalley for providing a review copy of this book!</i><br /><br />This review is also posted at <a href="http://t.co/NEOHhWm6" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Overdose</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5171329902577210033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_322010364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322010364" />
    <a title="Kadbury" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4789707-kadbury"><img alt="Kadbury" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1344771652p2/4789707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322010364?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kadbury" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kadbury" href="/user/show/4789707-kadbury">Kadbury</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789707-kadbury?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322010364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9952902907375152042">I loved Storm ,the first book in this series and I was dying to read this novel! I believe I squealed when I got accepted for this book.Needless to say my expectations for this book were sky high.<br/><br/>This is Gabriel and Layne's book. The entire book is told from their point of view.Chris and Becca do make an appearance but they're not the main characters in this novel.<br/><br/>I was a little disappointed with this book.The main reason I think I didn't like this book as much as Storm is because I wasn't a big</span>
  <span id="freeText9952902907375152042" style="display:none">I loved Storm ,the first book in this series and I was dying to read this novel! I believe I squealed when I got accepted for this book.Needless to say my expectations for this book were sky high.<br><br>This is Gabriel and Layne's book. The entire book is told from their point of view.Chris and Becca do make an appearance but they're not the main characters in this novel.<br><br>I was a little disappointed with this book.The main reason I think I didn't like this book as much as Storm is because I wasn't a big fan of Gabriel (Gabriel fans do not hurt me!).I just couldn't connect with Gabriel's urge to always be close to his element and the whole firefighting thing.I didn't hate Gabriel,I just couldn't understand him.I could see why he was so frustrated with his life.I couldn't form as much of a connection with Gabriel that I did with Chris and that's the only reason why I didn't enjoy this as much as Storm.Hunter annoyed me in this novel too.<br><br>I really liked Layne.I love the fact that Brigid creates such strong female characters! I hope Brigid keeps creating such strong characters because I love reading about them.Layne was a character I could relate to easily.She's the smart kid who's got some issues at home.I just loved the way the author revealed bits and pieces about Layne and had me guessing about what had happened with her .Recently in all the books I've read the female characters haven't been that great but Layne was a breath of fresh air.I loved reading about her.<br><br>The story was amazing and there was a twist at the end too.I couldn't put this book down! I got approved for this one when I was on vacation abroad and I was up late and couldn't put it down till I was finished! The best part is the fact that this book doesn't end with a cliffhanger but the sneak peak of Spirit ends with a KILLER cliffhanger.<br><br>My reaction at the end of the sneak peak<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/249565.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>[Word of advice: Start this book in the morning and DO NOT READ the sneak peak till you have the third book in your hand.]<br><br><i>Secondary Characters</i><br><br>I loved almost all the secondary characters in this novel.Especially loved Michael and Simon.<br><br>Dear <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4629194.Brigid_Kemmerer" title="Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Brigid Kemmerer</a> whatever you write I will buy.With this novel you have proved that you are not just a one time wonder and you can truly write great novels.<br><br>Overall,a fine addition to the series .I am eagerly waiting the release of Spirit (Book #3)<br><br>My Rating:<br>4/5<br><br><br><br><br>Note: If you're looking for something like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits" title="Pushing the Limits by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Pushing The Limits</a> .I think you will like this one a lot.I actually found some similarities to Pushing The Limits (This might have something to do with the fact that I read this book right after Pushing The Limits).There's a bad boy and damaged girl and lots of emotional trauma.<br><br><br><br><br><br><b>EDIT 28/8 </b><br><br>I got approved for this ! <br>FINALLY! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376544ra/731462.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2012">2012</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319612377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15969775165341682066">This series reminds me a lot of the Black Dagger Brotherhood series where each book showcases a brother’s story and their meet cute with their girlfriends. Naturally this is for the YA generation and is set in high school. Gabriel has a fiery “bad boy” image and like most of the stereotypical characters, he has a heart of gold. I was looking for something more? Maybe more of the paranormal elemental aspect instead of the kids and their relationship. I still love the brothers dynamics and I look </span>
  <span id="freeText15969775165341682066" style="display:none">This series reminds me a lot of the Black Dagger Brotherhood series where each book showcases a brother’s story and their meet cute with their girlfriends. Naturally this is for the YA generation and is set in high school. Gabriel has a fiery “bad boy” image and like most of the stereotypical characters, he has a heart of gold. I was looking for something more? Maybe more of the paranormal elemental aspect instead of the kids and their relationship. I still love the brothers dynamics and I look forward to reading about it in the next instalment. I just find these tortured characters are looking all the same. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15969775165341682066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>

<li class='cover' id='bookCover_15768191'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15768191-sweet-peril"><img alt="Sweet Peril (Sweet, #2)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1351223157l/15768191._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rGUS0mq0nVhOqr2w76XcXJbeK5nYhanJSN4uIOjFuACcvjx13ERPjRiUhHGTPc40a1vIfXXr6hV+svuUQuUWOQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wzMaQ5Ky0K8VNnBogqGwCwHzCPHTKYisDB4UE7GjYbDz6DTkJEICekMISan+OaJj/HbrFX5Hy3A6csGnG4PPiQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText2224192585303818406" style="display:none">Brigid Kemmerer is the New York Times bestselling author of dark and alluring Young Adult novels like A Curse So Dark and Lonely, More Than We Can Tell, and Letters to the Lost (Bloomsbury), as well as paranormal YA stories like The Elemental Series and Thicker Than Water (Kensington). A full time writer, Brigid lives in the Baltimore area with her husband, her boys, her dog, and her cat.
